et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if one delays cutting it until it is large, then take care if it is hard, of a livid color, and insensitive:
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	then do not touch it with iron, for it is a festering abscess, because when it is cut sometimes, great harm comes to the patient;
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not livid in color, and you see that it can be entirely cut, then empty the patient and cut it without fear, and treat the place with drying and astringent things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuity occurs in one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	Therefore, when this happens to someone, see if the wound is fresh with all its blood;
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then join the two lips with a suture, then treat it until it is healed;
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, you must scrape all the parts of their heart until they bleed, then bring the two lips together with a suture, and bind it, and sprinkle on dragon's blood powder and ground incense;
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	and place on the powders a piece of strong plaster or other consolidating plaster, and leave it until it falls off by itself, then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The manner of the suture is that you bring together the edges:
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or with needles, as we have said in the suture of the belly;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or with thread, as I have shown you.
des apostemes des levres	of the abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	In many men there occurs within the lips a hard abscess, similar to vesicles, some smaller and some larger;
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	then you must turn back the lips, and make an incision on each side, and grasp it with forceps and cut it in each part;
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	then fill the place after the incision with powdered vitriol, until the blood is stopped;
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then wash it with vinegar, and treat the place with drying things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	Of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Many times there grows on the gums added flesh, which the ancients call "albulus";
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	then you must hold it with tongs, and cut it at its root, and let the wound or blood run;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	then put on the place crushed vitriol, or other astringent and desiccative powders;
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if that flesh returns after the incision, and this often happens, then cut it a second time, and cauterize it:
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	it will not return after cautery;
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	and these are the forms of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of the sordes
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Sometimes there are gathered at the root of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, crusts which are foul and rough;
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	and sometimes the teeth are black and yellow and worm-eaten, until the corruption reaches the gum, and the teeth are foul-smelling;
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	then you must make the patient sit between your hands, and his head should be in your lap, and clean the teeth or the crusts which appear, until nothing remains;
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	and so do with the blackness and greenness, and the yellowness and other stains, until they are cleaned;
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	and if one removes what is there at the first scraping, it is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	if not, then begin again the second and third day, until you have cleaned everything;
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	and know that the teeth need various forms of instruments for cleaning, according to what the work demonstrates, because the scrapers with which one cleans outside the teeth have different forms than those with which one cleans between the teeth;
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	and these and other forms should be prepared and with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	It is necessary when you treat a toothache that you delay extraction as long as you can, for one should not do this;
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	for it is a very high substance until one has no excuse for scraping.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then, when the patient is compelled to extraction, it is necessary that you are certain of the aching tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Many times the pain deceives the patient, and he thinks it is in a healthy tooth, and has the good tooth extracted;
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and yet the pain does not depart because of that, until the bad one is extracted, for we have already seen this happen to these healers;
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	and when you are certain of the aching tooth, you must scrape around the tooth with a very strong spatula to protect the gum on all sides;
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then move it with your fingers or with fine forceps little by little, until it is well loosened, then firmly attach the forceps;
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and let the patient's head be on your lap between your knees, and hold it well so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	Afterwards, extract the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take one of these instruments and put it inside from each side lightly, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if the tooth is pierced and eaten away, you must fill it with lint where the holes are;
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and extract it carefully with forceps, so that it does not break on extraction;
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	and it is necessary to work very wisely around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And I warn you well that you do not break it, and that a part remains, and that greater pain than the first returns to the patient through the malice of the root.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And beware that you do not act as ignorant surgeons do, who through their haste and boldness sometimes break the tooth, and do not achieve what we have recounted;
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but sometimes cause, through the breaking of the tooth, or because of the roots that remain, a great illness, as we have often seen;
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	And when the tooth is extracted, wash the place with wine or vinegar and salt;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, fill the place with crushed vitriol;
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	and if that does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The shapes of the instruments with which one moves the teeth first should have long points and thick handles, so that they do not bend when you extract the tooth;
et ce sont les formes:	and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be of thick members so that they do not bend when pulling, and let them be of well-made iron, and let them be toothed to hold the tooth.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root remains after pulling, it is necessary that you place on the spot cotton moistened in butter for one or two days, until the place is softened, then put there the pincers which are called "algefri", of which the head resembles a bird's beak;
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	and let them be made inside like a file, and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pincers, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh all around the root, and put there the instrument which is called "althali", that is to say, a lever, of which this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root comes out by this, it is good;
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	if not, help yourself with all the instruments, of which the forms come here after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And one helps oneself with this instrument which has two prongs, of which this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and of other tools which are in front in the arrangement of teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large pincers, of which this is the shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And let this instrument be strong so that it cannot break, and know that there are many instruments for teeth;
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also other instruments, which are not counted;
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and the wise and subtle master finds his own instrument, according to what his work and the illness show him, for there are such illnesses where the ancients taught no instrument because of the diversity of cases; and if one breaks a piece of the cart [presumably, referring to the bones of the body] or other bones, or if it rots, then he seeks among the instruments which are necessary, that I have told you, and he helps himself with the gestures, of which this is the shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let them be thick and well-holding to hold the bone, so that it does not escape, but that one can hold and remove it;
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	and then restore the place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is rot in the bone, and it is small, then scrape it with this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the teeth appear not according to their natural course, and the form is ugly, and especially in virgin women, then you must know if the tooth is born after the tooth, and is not in the right place, and one cannot move it or file it:
adonques lou raie;	then shave it;
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	and if it is close to the tooth, then take this instrument of which here is the form, and it is similar to a small beak, and let it be of iron, sharp at the tip:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And cut it little by little over several days because of the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it is apparent that one can file it, then file it with a file such as this is the form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and it is like the file with which needles are made;
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	and file the tooth little by little over several days lightly, so that it does not move until it falls;
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	then smooth it at the end with some kind of scraper, and if the tooth is too sharp and it injures the tongue, then it is necessary to file the roughness until it is even, so that it does not injure the tongue nor impair speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth loosen
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the front teeth loosen, either by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot bite into what he eats without them falling out, and you have treated them with astringent medicines, and that does not work;
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	then it is necessary to restrain them with a gold wire, for silver wire turns green and rots, but gold never changes;
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	and let the wire be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, according to the amount of space between the teeth;
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	and if you wish to straighten the teeth, take the wire and double it between the two healthy teeth, then place the ends between the moved teeth, if there is one or more, until you wisely reach a healthy tooth on the other side;
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	then begin the wrapping again to the point where you began, and restrain your hand subtly and wisely, so that it does not move;
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	and let your binding be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then cut the ends of the wire with pliers, and join them, and place them between the healthy tooth, and place it so that it does not injure the tongue;
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	and then leave it thus tightened as long as it can remain, and if it loosens, or the wire breaks, tighten it with another wire;
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	it will remain and serve thus its entire time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the straightening of the two healthy teeth, and of the two moved, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when the tooth falls out, one puts it back in its place, freshly, as we have said;
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and let no one interfere who is not wise and patient, and sometimes one makes the form of a tooth from cow bone, and one puts it in the place where it is missing, and one tightens it as we have said, and it remains and serves thus a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the frenulum of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	Sometimes this frenulum which comes from under the tongue is natural, that one is born thus;
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or by accident of a healed wound;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the operation is such that you open the patient's mouth, and have his head in your lap, and lift his tongue;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	then cut the nerve frenulum widely, so that the tongue is released from its constraint, and if there is hardness or a knot, and this is from a sudden wound, then insert the hook and cut widely that ligament;
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and take care that the incision is not too deep, because of the artery which is below;
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have done, lift [the area] with rosewater and vinegar, or with cold water, then place under the tongue a linen tent;
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and let the patient dress it each night, so that the wound cannot close.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if bleeding occurs, put crushed vitriol on the area;
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if the bleeding overcomes you, cauterize it with the lentiginous cautery, which is good for this;
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then treat it with another treatment until it is healed,
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see it of a dark or black color or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, then do not touch it, for it is cancer;
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if it is tending towards whitening, and there is moisture, then pour on onion juice, and lance it with a fine spatula, and cleanse it from one side and the other;
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	and if the bleeding overcomes you in your work, apply crushed vitriol until it is stanched, then return to your work until you have removed all the pus;
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then clean the place with vinegar and salt, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Of the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Sometimes there come within the throat swellings which are called "godath," and they are properly called the two tonsils, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then take heed:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	if this abscess is hard, little sensitive, and of a dusky color, then do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red and the root is large, then do not touch it with iron, also because of the flow of blood;
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but leave it until it is ripe, and then you will open it, or it will break by itself;
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	and if it is of a whitish color around, and the root is thin, then have the instrument ready for cutting, but first see if the hot abscess is calmed and appeased.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then make the patient sit before the sun, and his head should be in your lap, and the operator opens the mouth and the assistant takes it between his hands, and presses the tongue down with the instrument, of which this is the form;
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	and let it be of silver or of thin bronze like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	When you press the tongue with this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the onion and stick it into the tonsil, and pull it out above as much as you can;
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	and pull out some of the membranes with it, then cut it with the instrument, of which this is the form, which resembles a pair of forceps;
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	and yet the ends are curved, and one towards the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of Indian iron or bronze:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, then cut it with pincers, of which this is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And let it be sharp on one side, and blunt on the other;
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and when you have cut one of the tonsils, cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision let the patient gargle with warm water, and vinegar and water, and if bleeding occurs, let the patient gargle with water in which pomegranate bark has been boiled, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding is stopped;
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it until it is healed;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	and sometimes other abscesses grow in the throat besides the two tonsils, then cut them in the same way as the two tonsils exactly.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman with an abscess which had grown inside her throat, that is to say, a small abscess;
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and it had almost completely closed her throat, so that the woman could not breathe because the passage was blocked, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained thus for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had risen so much that it had forced out two veins through the two nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I hastened then at once, and inserted a small hook into one, then pulled it out, and drew out a large portion of pus;
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	then I did likewise in the other nostril, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue;
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	afterwards I inserted the hook into the abscess, and cut a part of it, and only a little blood came out;
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	and thus the passage of the woman's throat was cleared, and she immediately began to drink water and then wine, and I did not cease cutting that abscess for a long time;
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	and the abscess grew again, and filled the space that I had emptied, until it was very large;
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	then I incised it and cauterized it inside the throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	thus it remained without growing;
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	and I departed from those parts, and I do not know what God did with her after me.
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When catarrh descends to the uvula, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular";
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if it is thick and round below, it is called "uve".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the heat of the abscess is subsided, and it is thin, then you must cut it;
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and that which is round and gathered and is not long;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and it is bloody or of a dark color or black, then you should avoid cutting it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and length, you must make the patient sit before the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument of which we have made mention before;
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	then insert the oncin into the uvula, and pull it down, and cut it with one of the two instruments that I have mentioned in the incision of the two tonsils.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And you must not cut more than the superfluity which is beyond the natural limit;
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	for if you cut more, you will harm the voice and speech;
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two tonsils, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient fears the cutting, then you must use a method of cauterization so that he does not feel pain.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is with sharp water.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And it is that the patient should put his head in your lap, and then press his tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and cauterize it with warm spring water, so that it is neither too thick nor too thin;
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and use the end of this instrument, of which this is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And it has on the head a cavity where one puts the medicine, like the bowl of a spoon, and puts the instrument with all the medicine on the uvula;
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and the patient should lie on his side, so that the saliva and mucus run from his mouth away from the medicine, so that it does not descend to the throat and injure it;
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	then hold your hand with all the medicine and press it on the uvula, the amount of half an hour, until you see it numb and the burning from the medicine is calmed;
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	and if you wish, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and wet the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument with all the cotton in the throat above, until the cotton touches the uvula;
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	and do this often, until the cautery is complete, then let it dry, and it falls after four or five days.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you need to restart the cautery with the medicine, then restart it, and after the cautery wipe around the uvula with cotton wrapped in butter, and clean what is around the medicine;
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let it be rinsed with cold water, and let it be treated with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This treatment is safer than incision, or than cautery;
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	if it is treated by fumigation in this manner, take calamint and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and vervain and similar herbs, and mix all or some of them in a pot, and add vinegar, and bring to a boil;
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and inside the pot there should be a perforated instrument according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And let it be of silver or bronze, and let one of the ends be placed in the mouth of the patient so that the vapor rises to the uvula through the throat, until the uvula is cauterized;
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	afterwards repeat it often, until the uvula is dry, and take care that you do not do this at the beginning of the appearance of the hot abscess, for many things happen there;
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and do not do this except at the decline of the hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not present, take a tube and put inside it an eggshell, so that the patient's mouth is not too hot;
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	for the eggshell does not allow the vapor to burn the mouth, and this is a good treatment and also a salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Many times a bone or fish spine, or something else, gets stuck in the throat;
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	then you must pull out what you can see, and press the tongue down with the instrument, so that you see the thing move;
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	and what you do not see and is lodged in the throat, you must make the patient vomit before the food is cooked in the stomach;
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	perhaps the thing will come out through vomiting;
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and tie a thread to the sponge, and then swallow it;
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when it comes to the place, it will stick, and then pull it out;
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come out by what we have said, take a lead instrument according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it may more easily enter the throat, and have the head raised high;
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest a cough comes to him, nor thrust the bone inside;
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	and it is better that the patient inserts the instrument, because he knows better where the thing is stuck;
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	then push it down, or pull it out with the instrument evenly, until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	Of the leech in the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	Sometimes the leech is medicated, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	and when that does not help, then look in the patient's throat at the sun, then press his tongue with the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the leech, pull it out with a small hook, or with fine forceps that are good for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that is not effective, take a horsehair, and put it in the patient's throat, then put a hot iron at the end of the hair, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And let the patient drink water every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	Then take a full glass of cold water, and open the mouth, and pour it in without swallowing, and move it around with your hand often;
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and as soon as the leech feels the water, it falls off.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not fall off as we have said, fumigate the patient with asafoetida, with the instrument that I have described in the fumigation of the uvula;
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	do this many times, for it will fall off without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the method of fumigation is that you take a pot in which there are live coals, and the pot is covered with a lid pierced in the middle, and in that hole is the end of the instrument;
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	then throw in your fumigation, and the patient puts the end of the tube in his mouth, and closes his mouth, so that the smoke does not escape, but comes down to the leech;
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	and the leech will fall off immediately, and if it does not fall off, repeat the fumigation many times;
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty and sharp things, and not drink water;
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	and then it will be necessary for it to come out forcefully through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the shape of the instrument with which one pulls out the leech is, when one can see it, similar to curved pincers to easily enter the throat;
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	and it resembles a bird's beak, and has a roughness like a file, so that what it grasps, it cannot let go;
et vez ci la forme:	and here is the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Many kinds of abscesses exist, according to what is remembered later in this book about one and another, and they differ in perforation and size;
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and this is in two ways, one of which is in its very appearance, and what it contains in moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is because of the places where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For abscesses of the head are different from those of the fundament, and abscesses of fleshy places are different from those that occur in joints, and each has its own judgment in treatment.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And there are abscesses that one should not pierce until the swelling is ripe according to its completion;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and there are some that it is necessary to pierce when they are grown, and do not mature according to their completion, such as abscesses that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses occur near joints, and one leaves them until they are rotten around, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	Or, if the abscess is near the principal member, and you delay perforation until it is ripe, it will harm the principal member;
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	or if it is near the fundament, one pierces it before it is ripe;
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	and it is not necessary that you pierce an unripe abscess without complete digestion, except that which is near the fundament, lest it rot deeply, and lengthen inward, and a fistula forms there;
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And it is necessary that you know the time of the perforation of the ripe abscess according to its completion, and that is when the pain is lessened, and the departure of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and of the throbbing and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs;
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and it is necessary that you make the perforation in the most dependent part of the abscess, and where it appears soft;
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and let the perforation be along the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and near nerves and arteries, and in all similar places where there is no bending.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that bend, along that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when the abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better that you delay the perforation until it is confirmed in completed digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce it before that, the body of the venom will be spread from it, and it is full of much filth;
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and perhaps the lips and depths of it will harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is an abscess that is pierced according to the breadth of the body, according to what the limb needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And it is necessary that you make small holes in small abscesses;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in large abscesses, large holes, and many fissures according to the resemblance of the size of the abscess;
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and there are such abscesses where it is necessary to reach the core, and to cut;
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	when it has become like a rag, and is dead, it is necessary to do as one does with buboes:
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and there are some that are split into three angles, and there are some that are cut like a myrtle leaf, like abscesses of the angles;
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and there are some where one makes a round incision, and other incisions and similar cuts.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those which have no head, like a superficial soft abscess, it is necessary that you pierce it completely;
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and it has collected much pus, and you pierce it, not to draw all the pus at that time, but to draw a part;
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	then stuff the abscess until the next day, then draw out something again;
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	do this many times gradually, until all the pus comes out;
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	especially if the patient is of weak constitution, or a pregnant woman, or a small child, or an old decrepit man.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirit sometimes leaps with the exit of the pus, so that by chance the patient dies, and you are not to blame.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Therefore perform this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived your abscess, clean the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small;
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it is a full incision, apply tents of linen or old cotton;
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, then you must place a tent in each so that they meet one another;
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	and if you have cut a part of the skin in the abscess, and you have turned it over, then you must fill it with old cotton or linen cloth shavings without moisture, and bind it until the third day;
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then remove it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs in your work, apply cold water and vinegar, and moisten a cloth, and apply it to the bleeding area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the bleeding persists, apply the treatment and remedies, and the powders that I have mentioned elsewhere in this book, and if it is winter, and the place where the abscess is is very sensitive, then you must apply tents and cloths moistened in wine and warm oil;
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	and if it is summer, and the place is fleshy, then you must apply cloths moistened in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil, until the third day, as we have said;
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then open the abscess and clean it and treat it, as is necessary, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And this must be universally known in the treatment of abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	I have told you how one should proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	In the scalp come small abscesses, and there are kinds that are web-like, like the comb of a hen, and there are many similar ones.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are fatty ones and others where there is moisture, like pus;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	and there are some that are hard and stony to the touch, and there is no doubt if the artery does not interfere.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the incision is that you should probe with the instrument which is called "entromissoire," whose form is given below, what thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then lance it from above lengthwise.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is emptied, then scrape it without leaving anything of the skin that contains that moisture, for it returns repeatedly when one leaves anything there;
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day;
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	and this will drain what remains from the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then repeat the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that nothing remains from the night;
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the wound with a suitable ointment, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess contains thick pus, cut it lengthwise, according to this form;
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and put in your ointments, and scrape it from all sides, and put all your effort into drawing the pus out of the pocket where it lies;
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	and if the artery opposes you, then do what I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And do the same with the abscess if it is stony, and with the cutting and cleaning as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the incision on a stony and moist abscess is easier, for they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if there are some of these abscesses on the head where there is no moisture, and among these were abscesses that I cut on the head of an old woman;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and I found the abscess like a hard, rough, and white stone, and could not break it;
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if one had struck it, one would have made a wound as well as with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses occurring on the head, except for those which appear on the heads of children and at the roots of the ears, the opening should always be at the lowest point, so that the matter may escape;
et les cure si com il covient.	and treat them as is necessary.
des scrophules	of the scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Often these abscesses occur in the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they appear elsewhere on the body, and are many, and are interconnected with one another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each scrofula is properly within its own sheath, like the nut and the abscess of the head, as we have said;
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and the appearances of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are malignant ones that do not want to obey treatment.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	In that one then which you see to be of good disposition to the touch, and is similar in color to the body, and moves on every side and is not close to the nerves of the neck nor to the artery nor to the windpipe, and is not deep;
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	then you should cut it from above, and scrape it from each side, and extend the two lips of the heart with hooks, if you need to, as we have said in abscesses of the head;
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	and draw it little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and that the spatula is not sharp or cutting, lest the hand slip, and do not go too far, lest you cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cut the vein or the artery, and that does not allow you to work, then put in the wound crushed vitriol, or some powders that stop blood, and bind the wound;
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	and leave it until the abscess is calmed, and the wound is softened, and begins to fester.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the blood is stopped, then return to your work, until you complete it;
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	then search with your index finger if there remain any small scrophulae, cut and cleanse them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrophula, it is not necessary that you cut that scrophula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it fall off by itself, without harm;
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	then fill the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then dress it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut the whole scrophula, it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound, and sew them immediately, since there is no remaining superfluity because of the size of the scrophula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	then you must attend to cutting its root, and pull it out, and sew it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those scrofulas which contain superfluity, pierce them where they appear ripe;
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and pierce it like the one previously mentioned, downwards, then apply tents with ointment and similar things, so that it may corrupt that which remains of the corruption;
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when the wound is well cleansed, then treat it with ointment generating flesh, until it is healed.
de squinance	of quinsy
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancients said and spoke of the incision of the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those who have quinsy, it is necessary that the fissure of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be opened;
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	and that one not make aid by this, because all the veins and the lung of the sick person are near to those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in the two tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the lung, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis to avoid the loss which comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, we must cut it below three or four circles a small fissure across, between the two circles or by the amount of the fissure of the tonsil, not in the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and that place is so suitable for the section of the epiglottis that there is no flesh, and the vessels are far away.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he extend the skin of the throat with the hook, then cut the skin until he reaches the channel;
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and avoid the blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cut the tonsil, as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm of the channel which leaps forth through the place which is broken, and by the lack of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour has passed in which strangulation is feared, bring together the two lips of the wound of the throat, and sew it all alone without the cartilage;
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then administer medicines which cause flesh to grow, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that one should not do this until the throat is completely swollen, and the patient is judged to be dying, and lacks breath.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then one cuts the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	and for this reason the ancients ordered leaving the wound open until the malice of the illness has passed, and it passes in three days or in four. And then they ordered sewing the wound and treating it, until it was healed;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a young lady took a knife, and thrust it into her throat, and cut part of the channels of the lung;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to treat her, and found her as good as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound, and found the blood that had flowed from it, and I knew well that she had not cut a vein or duct except the throat, and the wind came out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hastened, and sewed the wound, and treated it until it was healed;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and nothing happened to the young lady except that she was hoarse, and afterwards returned to her usual state;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	therefore I say that in the incision of the epiglottis one need not fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called a "hernia of the throat", and is a large abscess the color of a yolk, and is very common in women;
et est selonc II manieres:	and is of two kinds:
naturez, et accidens;	natural, and accidental;
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	or natural has no remedy.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental is of two kinds, of which one resembles fat, and the other kind resembles an abscess which comes from an artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and if there is fear, and it is not necessary to operate with fire cautery except in that which is small, and prove and search it with the whole probe:
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it like a nut of fat, and it is not attached to any vein, cut it, as one cuts nuts, and draw it out with its covering, if there is any;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and search well all around, and treat it as is necessary, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	of nuts
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many kinds of nuts there are, of which I will describe all the similarities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And now it is necessary that I explain all the difference which is between a nut and an abscess.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that an abscess is accompanied by heat and fever, until the boiling is past, and the putrefaction is complete;
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	Then the fever and the heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With a nut there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains a cyst, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a pimple, and grows large;
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to two appearances, either greasy or moist, and many are in color as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the nut, that you first examine it with the instrument which is called "probe," according to what its form will show in the chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of the examination of the abscesses of the nuts is that you take the moistest place that you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers little by little, until you know that the instrument has reached the core, then that it should be according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then withdraw the probe, and take care what comes out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If running moisture escapes, what color it has, treat it as I have said of the other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the probe no moisture comes, know that it is fatty, then treat it in a cross, and take it with tweezers, and lightly scrape it on each side and guard the sheath in which it lies so that you draw it out whole with the nut;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot draw it out whole, then draw it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, the nut returns many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if a little remains, and the blood troubles you, fill the wound with some sharp corrosive powders, and clean the wound, and apply things that soothe a hot abscess, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed;
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the nut is large, sew the two lips of the wound, and treat it with that which generates flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	And if the throbbing vein is contrary or otherwise hastens you, fill the place with powdered vitriol, and leave it there two or three days, until the wound festers, and the boiling of the blood rests;
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then return to cut away what remained of the nut.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	Here are the forms of the instruments used, and there are three kinds:
grans et moien et petit;	large, medium, and small;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and there are three squares which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and there are three kinds:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	large, medium, and small, for encircling abscesses of fistula;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are like the needles with which one sews up sores, and are of yellow brass, or of iron, or of silver, and those which are yellow are worth more, and are more proven with black lead for encircling the curves of fistula;
et sont de III manieres:	and there are three kinds:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	large, medium, and small, according to the size of the width of the holes.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The shapes of the hooks are very similar, as you see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	large, medium, and small;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and there are hooks which have two curves of three kinds also;
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and there are hooks which have three curves, and are also of three kinds;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and there are hooks which have two curves, and hooks of only one curve, and are of three kinds;
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The heads of those with which one cuts are sharp, and there are some which do not cut except on one side, with which one scrapes the humours, so that one does not cut the vein or the nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and of these introducers, the blades are enclosed in sheaths, so that the patient does not feel them at the opening of the abscesses;
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three kinds:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	large, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and one uses them only in fleshy places, such as legs, and arms, and breasts, and in the armpits, and in similar places;
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and sometimes one makes another small instrument, similar to a fig-wood splinter, according to this form, with which one stops blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is sometimes placed in the place that heals the cutting of veins and arteries, and sometimes round according to this large form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, until they resemble the breasts of a woman;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, must do so according to this form, from this line b. down to g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape away the fat, and fill the wound with flesh-generating medicine, then bring together the two edges of the wound with a suture, and treat it until it is healed;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	and if the breast droops and is softened by its size as happens in women, cut it in two parts from above, through two similar incisions;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one is attached to the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line b. to line g.;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape the skin that is between the two edges, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about sutures and powders, and what is necessary in the treatment, until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely made, because the patient will not rest, or because of the flow of blood, then you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it until it consumes the remaining flesh and fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of the abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the armpits are kinds of hard scrofula where there are ribs, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those then which contain moisture must be cut according to this form, from line b to line g:
