et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	and it splits lengthwise, and is displaced inwards, and the patient feels pain at the site, and throbbing, and swelling where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above, until you are above the fracture;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and know what the fracture is and its shape;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	and if the fracture is only at the head, then set the fracture evenly, until it is of its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is lengthwise, or it is displaced inwards, then have the patient lie on his stomach, until the resetting of that fracture is prepared for you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have set it evenly, then apply the plaster, then place a splint of wood or horn, and bind the fracture so that it does not move;
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and fill the space under the ribs, until the binding is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side, or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if hot abscesses occur there, do not touch them until the hot abscesses are calmed, and apply what we have said before;
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then return to the restoration, and bind it as is necessary, if there is no bad accident;
et c’est li maniere.	and that is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of the fracture of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The shoulder joint is that which is between the elbow and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, then one must restore it according to one of the two methods:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	one of which is that you take a straight piece of wood of moderate thickness, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And tie two cords to the two ends, and hang them upwards, and let the patient sit on a seat;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	then place his broken arm on the wood, until it reaches the armpit, and has in the middle a curve of wood, then hang on some heavy thing or the assistant stretches it downwards;
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	then let the surgeon place the fracture evenly with his hands together, until the fracture returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that one suspends the patient on his bed, and ties his hand to his neck, then instructs two assistants that one holds what is above the fracture with his hands, and the other holds below with a rope, and each stretches to his part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you want the traction to be stronger, then tighten one rope below the fracture, and above the fracture, and let each of the assistants stretch to his part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the fracture is close to the head of the shoulder, then you must place one rope in the middle under the armpit, and another towards the elbow, under the fracture;
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	and also if the fracture is towards the elbow, then you must place a rope lightly, without effort, until the fracture is even on the place, and on the elbow;
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	then set the fracture evenly, as is necessary, and tighten it, if no hot abscesses appear.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if hot abscesses appear, then do not tighten it until seven days, and apply wool soaked in vinegar and rose oil, until the hot abscesses are calmed;
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	then tighten it, and the manner of tightening is that you place the plaster on the fracture, then assemble the arm to the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the breast;
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and place the cloth, and tighten it on the shoulder and on the arm, so that the arm is in its proper place, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone might move, then use splints, and place on the fracture one splint larger and stronger than the others, and let there be one finger's breadth of space between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it surpasses the fracture by three finger breadths on each side;
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	then tighten the splints, as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the fracture, more strongly and less as you move away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the placement of the splints, and the tightening, as we have said, at the time that you restore the broken limb, and you suspect a hot abscess, then leave it to ripen until the seventh day, as we have said;
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	then examine every three days the bandage, that an itching or swelling does not come there, or that nourishment cannot reach the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If so, correct it, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if no such accident occurs, then do not unbind it except after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, and have his hands on his stomach;
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and place under the shoulder a cushion filled evenly with wool, and check every hour of the day or night, that the shape of the broken limb does not move, or that the bandages are not loosened;
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	then correct it by the virtue of medicine, and give him the food that we have mentioned before, in such a way that the food is at first subtle;
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when he begins to recover, let it be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be healed within forty days altogether;
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and then one should unbind it and administer baths and ointments to heal the place.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is severe and swollen, it remains unbound for fifty days or two months.
de la brisure du bras	Of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the two "foscile", of which one is small, and it is the one that follows the elbow;
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is large, and it is the one that is below, towards the little finger;
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	by chance the large foscile is broken alone, or the small one, and by chance both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small foscile is broken, the restoration is easy, and the healing;
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	and when the large one is broken, the healing is difficult, and more serious than when both are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small foscile that is broken alone, then it should be slightly extended a little, and set even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it is the large foscile, then it should be pulled harder;
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and extend it on a cushion, and hold the little finger of the hand higher than the others, and the little toe lower than the other toes, and let the patient be crossed over himself, and a cushion in front of him higher, so that the patient suffers no pain;
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	then let the attendant extend his arm to the lower part of his hand, or to a ligature, and another attendant to the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then let the physician set it even, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture there are pieces, then put each one in its place, and if there is any separated that touches the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then cut it off and remove it, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken of it in a separate chapter;
si pren la cure.	then take care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if at the beginning of the restoration, hot abscesses occur, then glue a cloth of cerote made of rose oil and white wax, which is neither too hard nor too soft;
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and bind the cloth on subtly, until the hot abscesses are calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	And then remove the cerote, and apply a plaster of the mill powder with abundant egg, then apply the splints, and let the splint of the fracture always be stronger, and a little wider than the others;
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and know that there should be six splints on the arm in several arrangements:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	whether the fracture is in one of the bones, or in two;
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and bind more tightly above the fracture than elsewhere, and always less tightly as it moves away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter;
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and let the cloths that are over the fracture be soft and moist, and not hard or rough;
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and let the thread, with which it is bound, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And examine the limb and the binding after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if any bad accident happens to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you must bathe the limb with warm water until that itching is calmed;
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and do not let the limb rest tightly.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then recommence the binding, and if the binding is loosened and the bone separated, and similar things, then correct it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And then take care that nourishment can reach the limb, for if it is too tight, you must loosen it a little, and leave it so for a few days until nourishment flows there, and then tighten it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said happens to the patient, then do not unbind it until twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	or around, then hang his hands around his neck, and let his neck be straight, and beware of movement and fidgeting, and sleep on his back;
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and know that this fracture is healed in thirty or thirty-five days, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	Of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and in the knuckles of the fingers, few fractures occur, and only bending happens many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the palm of the hand is broken or bent, the patient must sit cross-legged, and sit straight before him equally;
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	then he places his hand on the extended cloth, and the attendant extends the broken bones, and places them equally aligned, until they are well joined;
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	and applies the plaster and the lint, if no abscess forms, then applies a splint according to the size of the area;
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and it should be wrapped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the fracture is on the inside around the palm of the hand, make a sling of cloths, and instruct the patient to hold it to his broken palm;
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	and then binds it with a long cloth, and let the splint be soft leather as large as the palm of the hand, and bind it, as is necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is on the outside, you must place one splint on top, and another underneath on the palm, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie it all around the hand, and tighten the binding between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if the fracture occurs in any of the knuckles of the fingers, if it is the thumb, set it straight, as is necessary;
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and bind it with the palm, and if you wish, place a small straight splint to lift the fracture, and it will not move;
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	and if the fracture is in the other fingers, such as the index finger or one of the others, set it straight, and bind it with the healthy finger that is next to it;
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	or you bind them all together in an "I" shape, whichever works better, or you place a splint on top, as with the thumb;
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	and take care in the restoration and in the preparation of a hot abscess, and help what comes from it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The thigh bone is often broken, and one sees it well when it turns forward and backward;
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	and the restoration is that one binds one ligature above the fracture, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patient lies on his face, then each attendant extends his ligature to his part equally;
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and this is when the fracture is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is close to the root of the thigh, let one of the ligatures be towards the groin, and the other ligature below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And similarly if it is close to the knee, then let the ligature be near the knee, and let the extension be below;
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	then let the surgeon set the bone equally with his two hands, until it is according to its natural form, and then apply the plaster, and bind it, if no abscesses form there.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside, then return to your work and your treatment;
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The ligature is made in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	It is necessary that you wrap around the fracture a hard bandage doubled in two or three, and the excess remains, then turn the leg until the heel comes to the root of the buttock, and put a long thread between the thigh and the leg, near the knee below, and let the ends of the thread come to the top;
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	then turn the bandage over the leg and over the thigh, then place splints over the fracture, and place a splint over the bone of the leg;
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	then fill the empty space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloths to make the tightening even, then begin to tie firmly three or four turns above the fracture;
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	and the further you go above the fracture, the less you tighten it;
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	then take the two ends of the thread that you placed between the leg and the thigh, and tie the three splints that are above, then return below to the end of the thread, until you come near the foot;
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, until neither abscess nor swelling nor anything similar appears.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if it happens, then untie it, and treat what has appeared, as we have said many times;
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if there are pieces of bone that prick, it is necessary to remove them, if one can;
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	and if one cannot, then it is necessary to cut open the place, and pull it out forcefully;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And sometimes the thigh is broken so that splints are applied, as in the shoulder and arm;
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	nevertheless, in the restoration thus made, the patient does not limp.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in L days, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversities of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the kneecap
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the kneecap there is little fracture, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is only a fissure, or a hole, and it happens with a wound, and without a wound, and this one feels well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is that one puts what is round to its sides equal, until it is assembled as much as one can;
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	then put the plaster, and put a round splint there, if you need it, and bind it as is necessary, then observe all the conditions that we have mentioned in other fractures, such as hot abscess and other similar things;
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply to each accident what is necessary for it, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is rightly called "mustelz", and the other is called "foscile";
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	and the same fracture occurs as in the arm, and therefore the restoration is the same as that of the arm, and the procedure is entirely similar. And if the two bones are broken together, the leg turns in every direction.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thin bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it is clearly visible;
et torne desoz.	and it turns downwards.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Then administer extension, and set it straight, and bind the splints evenly;
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	but however, if the fracture is severe, and there are several pieces, the extension must be gentler and lighter;
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and ease it according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have completed your work, take two wooden splints that encompass the leg on either side, and are the length of the leg from the knee downwards;
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	then wrap around it in two places a bandage above and below, and bind it in the middle also, and with this binding the leg cannot deviate to the right or left, and so it is well;
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	and some administer a splint the length of the leg, which is made of wood, and in it the leg is placed to prevent movement, and this is properly done in a fracture where there is a wound;
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	and move the leg each day, to see if there is a hot abscess or other complication;
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, fracture does not occur, but at the bones of the foot fracture sometimes occurs and at the toes also, and there is only a crack in several ways.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if a fracture occurs in the bones of the foot, and you see these bones overriding each other, then have the patient put his foot on the ground, as if he wanted to walk, and then immediately put your foot on his, where the bones are raised, then press it until they return to their place;
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	then apply the plaster and lint, and place under the sole of the foot a small board with two full ends, then bind it to the foot properly, after you have wrapped cloths around it, and other things that you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, untie the binding, for you will find the bones even, whether fractured or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if any of the toes are broken, restore them as we have said for the fingers of the hand;
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	then place on the broken toe a splint according to the length of the toe, and let it be a little wider, then place under the foot that board which I have mentioned, and bind it properly;
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	and if there are two or three, or more, broken, then place on each toe a splint according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and bind the board under the foot;
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	and let it rest on the head of the board above the belly of the foot, so that it holds it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And you must not forget the other things that I have said for other fractures, as we have said;
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	and treat each accident as is necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the wrist
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bone of a woman's nature is broken, make her sit upright, then incline her to the back, and let her be held from behind;
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	then fill the vagina of the patient with cotton, and put in as much as will fit;
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	then stand the woman up, and lift her back little by little, and then the cotton will come out, until it reaches the entrance of the vagina, and the bone will return with the cotton;
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, replace it, and do this for seven days or thereabouts:
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	the fracture will be restored, and if you wish, take a sheep's bladder, and tie a string to the opening, and put the whole bladder into the vagina;
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	then blow strongly into the string until the bladder is inflated inside;
la nature si revenra li brisure;	the fracture will then be restored to its natural position;
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then it should be filled with cotton, and leave it like that for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bone of a man's or woman's wrist is broken, restore it in the same way as we have described for the hip bone;
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	and these fractures are not hidden from one who studies and practices them, and attends to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the fracture signifies in many ways the correct method of restoration:
enten le donques.	understand it then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's neck and put the penis in it;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	then wrap cloths around it, and leave it for three days or however long it takes, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	Of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for someone who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is large, such as a bone in the thigh or shoulder or similar, that he be healed immediately, so that the healings that we have described testify to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then stop it with vitriol, if you have nothing else, then begin again to restore the fracture at that same time, or that day, if hot abscesses do not appear.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if hot abscesses appear, then leave the restoration until the ninth day, until the abscesses are subsided, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would cause bad consequences.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is apparent on the uncovered flesh, then you must put it in place lightly with your hands, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if extension is not suitable for you to put it in place with your hands, then reset it with this iron instrument, which is seven or eight fingers long, and its width is according to the size of the wound;
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and for this reason it is necessary for the surgeon to have three or four, according to what he needs for each treatment of a fracture;
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and let it be round and somewhat thick, so that it does not bend under compression on the limb during your work, and let it be sharp in front, and thick from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	And it is called a "palainche," therefore the curved head should be placed on the head of the apparent bone;
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	and push it at once, until it returns, and is even one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot easily grasp the bone, then you must cut the head of the bone, until the instrument has power over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot reset the bone, as we have said, then cut it with an instrument suitable for this, either an incisor or a saw, as you are able;
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	then clean that which remains on the bone of roughness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	Then do what is necessary so that it is in its place, then moisten a cloth in black styptic wine, and properly if it is summer;
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and do not put on the wound cerate or anything else where there is oil, lest it cause putrefaction and corruption;
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	then administer stitches when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut the covering all around, according to the size of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not constricted with the fracture;
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	and many times foolish surgeons have done this, and have caused the patient death or corrosion sometimes;
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	and let the bandages be softer and smoother than for other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is bad or large, and you fear that bad complications may arise, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then you should not put stitches there;
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	but wrap around, instead of stitches, hard cloths, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days, proud flesh forming on the wound, then remove everything you have put on with wine, and apply an ointment that heals wounds, such as tetrafarmacum ointment and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must unbind the limb twice a day, morning and evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be positioned in such a way that the proud flesh runs down slightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass, and it cannot heal but keeps producing proud flesh, know that there are small pieces of bone, wherefore you must probe the wound with a tent, and remove all those separated pieces which cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula develops there, or another kind of corruption, then you must treat it, according to what is said in the chapter before this.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when the bone is broken, and open on the limb, like the bone of the thigh or the shoulder, and others similar of the great limbs, do not remove it, for many times death results, but leave it until it rots;
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	perhaps it will fall out by itself after twenty or thirty days, then cure the wound, if you can;
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of the swellings that come upon the suture
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	Many swellings come after the healing of the fracture, especially when it is near the joint, and the appearance of the limb is an ugly thing to see;
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	and perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Take care then if the bone is fresh:
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	administer styptic medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocol, acacia, and similar others, so that you take some of these things, or all together, and mix them with styptic wine or with egg white or with vinegar;
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and apply them to the wound on lint, and bind it tightly, and do not unbind it for several days;
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	and then unbind it, and begin again with another, until the inflammation is gone;
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	or you bind on a well-made piece of lead;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	for the property of lead is that it removes all swellings from the limbs;
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	and if the inflammation has already turned to hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cut it open, and remove the excess that is visible;
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	or you scrape it with a razor until it is removed, and treat it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb which is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the fracture of the bone is healed, and the limb remains weak and thin afterwards, this happens for many reasons:
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	one of which is that it was bound too tightly, and was not bound as it should have been;
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	or because there were too many bandages, and nourishment could not reach the limb;
ou por multitude d’arosement;	or because of excessive inflammation;
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	or because of too much movement, not at the proper time;
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	or because he has little blood in his body, and is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body soft, until the blood is multiplied in him;
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and administer baths, and give him joy and gladness;
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	then put poultices on the limb, so that the poultices draw great nourishment to it, and often moisten it with warm water, until the nourishment flows to the limb;
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and returns to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the limb twisted after the healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the limb is twisted after the restoration, and the broken bone is apparent, and the shape of the limb is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural function:
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	do not believe the fools who say that one should break the limb again, and many foolish people have done this in our land;
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and this practice is blamed, and great harm comes from it, and perhaps death;
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	however, if the knots and the stiffness are fresh, then they should be bathed in warm water, or softening herbs should be cooked, such as mallow leaves, and roots, and melilot, and similar things;
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	and make a softening plaster, such as well-made diachylon, and you take the mucilage of mallow, and cook it with hen grease or sesame oil, and make a plaster on top;
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	or you take fat figs, and crush them with pigeon dung, and similar medicines that reduce the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the knot is removed by rubbing continuously and for a long time with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let movement be given to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the tortuosity is old and hardened, like stone, and it needs to be removed with iron, then it must be cut to the bone, with a fine, light scalpel;
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	and put care and diligence into the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When a dislocation occurs in someone, it must be immediately reduced without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if one delays, the place swells, and perhaps one can only reset it with difficulty;
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	therefore one must not move it when it is swollen:
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	often it causes spasms and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	however, when this happens, bleed the patient, then leave it until the abscesses are calmed;
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	then bathe the limb with warm water and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each limb as its treatment dictates.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from the head to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	It rarely happens that both jaws are dislocated, and the dislocation of both is according to two manners:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	or they are a little removed from their places, and softened a little;
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	or they are completely dislocated, and hang towards the breast, and the saliva runs from the mouth that he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, and his tongue is entangled with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by itself in several positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and accomplished, then you must reset it quickly, and not delay;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	and in such a manner that the assistant holds the head of the patient, and puts the little finger of one of his hands into the root of the dislocation of the mandible inside the mouth, if the dislocation is on two sides;
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and the other two fingers of the hands should be outside, to make it even;
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and instruct the patient to soften his jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the little finger places it evenly, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if the reduction is difficult, especially if it is the two mandibles together, then bathe them with warm water and oil, until you soften them slightly;
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	and do not delay in the reduction, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are reduced evenly, and the patient's mouth closes well without softening, then apply cloths moistened in a cerate made of rose oil and wax, then bind it lightly with soft bandages;
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and let the patient sleep on his back, and his head be supported between two cushions, so that he does not move it neither to the right nor to the left, nor strain to chew, but take light food, until the pains are gone, and the mandibles are healed;
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then he may eat what he wants lightly, and he should not strain to open his mouth when eating and drinking, until the mandible is well healed and sound.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be immediately reset, and are not returned to their place, then there comes fever and accustomed swelling, and perhaps looseness of the bowels, and perhaps vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see this, then know that it is perilous;
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	and many times he who this happens to dies within nine days.
de la forcelle	of the clavicle
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The clavicle cannot be dislocated inwards towards the continuation of itself and the breast, and it is sometimes dislocated outwards, and this is easily felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the restoration is such that the patient lies often on his back, and extends his arms;
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	and then press the place firmly with your palm, and it will return;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then apply the plaster and bandage it, and bind it tightly;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	and the head which is towards the rib cannot be dislocated;
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	unless slightly, and if it dislocates sometimes, then reset it in its place, as we have said;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	then apply the plaster and bandage it tightly, and instruct the patient to rest until healed;
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and in the same way is the head of the shoulder reset, when it is separated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	Know that the shoulder is dislocated only in three ways:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	one is that it dislocates towards the armpit below;
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	and the second is towards the breast;
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	and by chance it dislocates upwards, and this happens rarely;
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	and it does not dislocate backwards because of the shoulder, nor inwards because of the nerves;
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	and many times it dislocates downwards towards the armpit, especially in those who have little flesh, for in them it jumps easily;
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	in those who have enough flesh, it jumps with difficulty, and returns with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men that there is a percussion or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	Therefore, you must test it until you are certain;
et adonques encomence la cure.	and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And the dislocation is known when it is lowered towards the armpit, and it shows a difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a manifest difference between them;
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	and you will find a hollow at the head of the shoulder, and beneath the armpit, when touching the head of the shoulder, as if it were an egg;
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and the patient cannot bring his hand to his nose, nor move it in any way;
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you find it manifestly by touch;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this kind of dislocation is not difficult to reset, when it is recent, or if the child is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	And the method is that the attendant raises the patient's hand upwards, then places his fists under the armpit, and forcefully raises the joint upwards into place;
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	and the attendant raises the hand, and extends it upwards, then puts it downwards;
si venra hastanment.	it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if it does not come as we have said within a few days, then it is necessary that the patient be bathed in warm water;
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and the attendant should apply a softening and soothing poultice, such as a decoction of mallow, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and it should be administered;
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then the patient should be laid on his back, and a pad of wool of equal thickness should be placed under the armpit, neither too soft nor too hard, then the physician should place his heel on the pad, and gently raise the head of the shoulder, and pull the patient's hand;
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and another attendant should hold the patient's head, so that it does not move downwards;
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	that shoulder will return immediately, and if you wish, reset it in this manner:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and it is that you cause to be present one man who is larger than the patient;
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and let him be straight towards the side, and put his shoulder under the patient's armpit, and lift the armpit upwards, so that the patient hangs in the air;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	and another attendant pull the patient's hand downwards towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, let him hang with something heavy, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And it is reset also in another manner:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and that is, one sticks a long firebrand in the earth, of which the head should be as round as a pestle, and should be neither too thick nor too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	then it is placed under the patient, but so that he has soft cloths on top, and the patient stands along the length of the wood;
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	then let his hand be pulled down strongly on the other side, and the joint will return to its place quickly;
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	and if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, then do this treatment:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	take a firebrand of two spans long and four fingers wide, which has a round head to enter easily deeply under the armpit, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	then tie soft cloths to the head of the wood, so that the wood does not injure the patient, then place it under the armpit of the patient;
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	and extend his arm along the length of the wood, and tie the shoulder to the wood, and the arm at the wrist, then place the arm on a rung of a ladder that is wide, and let the hand be extended downwards, and let the body hang on the other side:
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	the joint will return immediately.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in, in whatever manner that may be, you must place under the armpit an equal ball of wool, then apply the plaster prepared with powdered millstone, with incense and egg white, over the whole shoulder and around, then bind it tightly under the armpit, and turn the bandage over the plaster, and clasp the hand to his neck, and let the hand remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And it is necessary that he eat little, until the limb is strengthened, for it will heal more quickly;
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then eat more after five or seven days, and move it;
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	and if it is firm and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place because of moisture that has entered, or for another reason, you must apply cautery to three points, as is described in the chapter on cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all this, and it loosens after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and he cannot raise his arm, then know that the nerves at the head of the shoulder are cut or stretched or softened;
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	The dislocation which is towards the breast and nipples, or behind, is caused by a blow and stretching of the hands, and another treatment is administered there;
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing there is stiffness in the limb, and slowness in movement, let the patient use a bath many times, until that stiffness is lessened, and it returns to its former nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the rib
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	Know that the joint of the rib is dislocated with difficulty, and returns with difficulty;
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	and it is dislocated on all sides, and especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not hidden, for one sees it well and feels it well;
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	and dislocated according to each form.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the diseased rib with the healthy one, you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is broken, and he cannot bend his arm, nor touch his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And you must reset it before hot abscesses come there, for if hot abscesses came there, it would be difficult to reset it;
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	and perhaps it cannot be reset at all, especially when it is at the back;
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	it is worse than other dislocations, and is more painful, and death may result.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	And the restoration is, when it is such that it can be reset, that you extend his hand with your two hands;
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	and his arms should be spread out, and the hands of the doctor around, above and below, and put the joint to its sockets together, or at the root of its palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and strikes the root of the palm where the dislocated joint is.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	And if it will not return to its place, administer strong extension;
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	and it is that two assistants extend the arm, and two assistants hold it, so that it does not move during the extension;
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	then turn the arm on each side, after you have wrapped a long and wide double cloth;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the physician joins the joint with his hand, he should anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then put the joint forcefully, until it returns;
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is in place, apply a dry plaster with egg white, and bind it firmly, and hang the arm around the patient's neck, and leave it for some days, then unbind it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	And if the joint is firm in its place, untie the binding, and leave it;
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	and if you see that the joint does not hold well, redo the plaster and the binding, and leave it like that for some days, until it is firmly set;
puis le deslie.	then unbind it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	And if he feels pain after the resetting of the joint, and it moves, bathe and rub it gently, and press until it is soothed;
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	or you put on the joint a poultice of fat mutton, then leave it one day and one night, then remove it, and make him enter the bath;
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	and when he sweats, rub the joint moderately, then put the poultice back on, and then enter the bath;
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and thus do it two or three times, until he is healed;
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	and if you wish, put on warm, moist cow dung mixed with butter, and bind it on;
si revenra a sa disposition.	then it will return to its proper place.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	The joint of the hand dislocates, and its reduction is easier than other joints.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	However, it must be returned to its place quickly, at the very moment it is dislocated, before the place is swollen, or a hot abscess forms there.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the reduction is that you place the affected hand on a table, and the assistant extends the hand, and positions it evenly, so that he places his palm on the appearance of the joint, and pushes until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	However, you must check if it is well in place;
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	then the patient places the back of his hand on a table during extension and reduction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, the patient places the back of his hand on the table, and the assistant places his hand on that part of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If it returns immediately, it is good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, restrain it with soothing plasters applied warm, and leave it thus without restarting.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot put it back in place after a few days, the joint remains crooked;
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	and it harms the patient not at all except that the hand is weakened, and cannot grasp anything at all:
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	then know that the nerves or arteries are severed;
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	there is no other remedy except to cauterize near the wound, and perhaps nothing else will help.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, apply the plaster we have described, then bandage it and leave it for five days, then unwrap it and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is any stiffness, moisten it with warm water, and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on either side, sometimes on the back of the palm or on the belly;
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	then extend the finger, and push the dislocation with your thumbs until it returns, then support the head of the finger, and bend it towards the part where it is disjointed;
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	and leave it for two days, and then set it even that day;
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	and at night bind it, as we have said, and unbind it by day, and make it move, and bind it at night;
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this often, until it is tight, and do the same, if it is dislocated on the palm of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed;
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and do likewise, when it is dislocated elsewhere.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Of the dislocation of the spine of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine of the back or neck is dislocated, or if there are several dislocations, there is no cure, for death quickly takes the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	And the sign is that excrement leaps forth without will, nor can he hold it, and often some limbs are softened, whether the two thighs, or the two arms, or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	And many times the spine moves in four directions;
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	That which moves backward is called "gibbosity":
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	The cure is that you observe if the gibbosity came from infancy:
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	then there is no cure or healing at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from a fall or from blows or similar things, the ancients described methods of cures with grand words, where there is not much benefit in all;
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have devised instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the gibbosity that comes to the breast in front, there is no remedy nor health;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and also that which comes straight to the two sides, and one cannot cure except that which properly comes to the back, as I say;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and it is that the patient be stretched on his face in a level place, and have a cushion beneath him, that he not be injured;
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then stick a firebrand firmly in the ground at the head, and another at the feet, and tie a rope across the patient's armpits, and another at the hips, and knees, and ankles;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	and two assistants hold the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two firebrands;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and let them be well secured, the firebrands as we have said, and the physician place his palms firmly on the spine, until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return by this treatment, then take a board three arms long, and place it under the wall, and let the patient be on his side, and place the end of the board under the wall, then place the middle of the board on the spine;
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	and let the physician place his feet on the other end of the board, and press firmly, until it returns to its place;
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and if you wish, do it with a lathe that turns by hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And it is that you place two firebrands at the head of the patient a cubit apart, and towards the feet two others, and let there be between each firebrand, above and below, a palm's breadth of space;
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	and let there be in each firebrand one hole, where the lathe runs, and let the firebrands be firmly in the ground, so that they do not move;
