et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and between each two firebrands let there be one turning firebrand, upon which the cords turn, and let there be on the two turning firebrands two small firebrands a palm's length long, to turn the lathe;
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then tie the cord which is through the armpits to the lathe towards the head, and the other cord towards the feet to the other lathe, and each of the assistants turns his lathe with the whole cord, and the master places the spine evenly as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is even, then put on a drying plaster with egg white, and then the lint, and then the splint of a tablet three fingers long, which covers the place of the gibbosity and the part of the healthy spine, then bind it with a cord, as we have said, and let the patient use a light diet, until he is healed;
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	and if anything comes at the end of the healing, then it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the splint that we have mentioned above;
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	and sometimes one administers a piece of lead, and sometimes the appearance comes in the posterior spine of the back, and one thinks that it is a dislocation;
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	and it is the bone that appears, wherefore one should not have presumption there:
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	by chance it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of the dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	Know that at the joints of the hip and at the joints of the shoulder, only dislocations occur, not as in the other joints;
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	and the hip joint is dislocated in four ways:
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	inwards and outwards, and forwards and backwards;
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	and more inwards than elsewhere, and slightly dislocated forwards and backwards.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the recognition of its inward dislocation is that when one joins the diseased leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the diseased knee is more open than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend his knee to the fire;
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and the place which is nearby is swollen with a hot abscess, because the head of the thigh comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of that which comes outwards, is that these symptoms are contrary to those above.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	And the signs of that which happens in front, are that he extends his leg well according to its length;
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	nevertheless, he does not bend his knee without pain, and if one wants to make it move, it cannot go forward, and he retains his urine, and his groin swells, and when he walks, he steps on his heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of that which happens behind, are that he cannot extend his knee, nor bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the groin is softened, and the head of the thigh is in the place under the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	The treatment of this type of dislocation is that you should observe if the dislocation is old, and if it remains according to its position, there is no cure;
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	and there is no need for presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	And in that where the dislocation is fresh, and it is of the four kinds of dislocation, hasten that you turn the joint, and extend it inwards and outwards, and move it to the right and left;
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	by chance it will return, and needs no other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this manner, then you must prepare a strong assistant, and extend the leg strongly with two hands, or with a linen cloth that is tied above the knee;
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	and another assistant extends his hand above in such a way that he puts his hands under his armpits, then grasps him with a soft cloth above the thigh;
et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another holds the head of the linen;
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and they extend upwards and downwards all at once, until the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to the four similar cases, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance.	If not, then it is necessary to treat it similarly.
Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	When the dislocation is inward, it is necessary that you place the patient on his healthy side, then place the linen on the root of the thigh, and the place which is under the groin, then extend the linen upwards towards the groin, and towards the shoulder;
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment:	then let another assistant take his arms, and embrace the large part of the affected thigh, and extend it outwards strongly;
si revenra a son leu maintenant;	then it will return to its place immediately;
et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	and this type of dislocation is easier than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot reduce it in this manner that we have described, it is necessary that you bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong, soft linen above the two heels, and above the two knees, and let the affected leg be extended two fingers more than the other;
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc;	then let it be hung from the top of a pole, and let it be two arms-lengths above the ground;
puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	then instruct an assistant to embrace the head of the thigh, and let another assistant hang with the patient, who firmly embraces the thigh, for the joint returns immediately and quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is outward, let the patient lie down, as we have said in the case of one who has a gibbosity, and draw a linen tightly around the affected leg properly, and also around the foot;
puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	then place two burning coals, one at the head and another at the feet, then insert a burning coal between the thighs of the patient in the middle of the groin;
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and have moistened cloths placed around, so that it does not burn the patient, then let each assistant stretch towards him, and let the physician place the dislocation equally with his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place it on a table, and press it as we have said in the case of gibbosity, and let the patient lie on his healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit;	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the affected leg quickly, and according to what I have said;
et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	and let the physician put his effort on the affected angle, then press with the other hand, and extend it downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches;	And if the dislocation is behind, it is not necessary to extend the affected limb downwards, nor to raise it from the ground, but it should be as if the hip were dislocated behind, as we have said about lying on the two hips;
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and let him be on his face, and the limb extended as we have said before, and one should press on the joint against the table;
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz;	and it will be right when the patient extends his legs, and they are equal;
adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	then join the thighs, and apply the plaster, and bind it with a bandage, so that the hip does not move;
et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus;	and let it rest for three or four days, then unbind it, and apply the plaster again;
et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors;	and if you see that they are equal, then bind it, as before, and leave it for three days;
puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	then unbind it, and make him walk gently, until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres:	The knee is dislocated in three ways:
c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier;	that is to say, inwards and outwards, and backwards;
et ne desalue point devant.	and it does not dislocate forwards.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the sign is that you instruct the patient to bend his leg to his thigh, and if it does not bend to his thigh, know that it is dislocated;
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back against his face, and place his foot on your feet;
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment;	then take his knee in your palms, and pull it between your fingers, then bend the two sides of the knee strongly;
et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	and another assistant extends his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he bends his leg easily to his thigh;
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie;	and apply the plaster, and bind the leg to the thigh, and bind them together tightly for three or four days, then unbind it;
et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and the patient should not exert himself to walk, until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not straight, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is sometimes displaced, and sometimes completely dislocated, both inwards and outwards.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the sign is that the ankle is swollen, and tense towards the part where it is dislocated:
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	The reduction is easy, and one should gently extend it with one's hands when it is only displaced.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is completely dislocated, you must make the patient sit upright, and hold him firmly by the leg, above the ankle;
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with your left hand twice, then extend it upwards, and gently place the foot upwards;
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	and do this twice, as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot;
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	If it returns, it is good;
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	if not, then begin the procedure again, for it will return;
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it cannot return thus, then make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and firmly fix a stake in the ground between his thighs, and tie cloths around it, so that it does not injure the patient;
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	then let the assistant hold the thigh, and another assistant extend the foot with his hands or with a strap, which he ties above the ankle;
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	then let each assistant extend equally, and the stake shall always be between the patient's thighs to restrain the patient when he is extended;
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	then let the surgeon equally set the dislocation with his hands, and another assistant hold the healthy leg underneath, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is in place, then apply the plaster and lint, and bind it firmly, and tie the foot to the leg, and guard the nerves which are on the ankle behind, that the binding not be too tight;
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	then leave it two or three days, and if the binding loosens, then tighten it;
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	then unbind it on the third or fourth day, and forbid the patient from walking for four days;
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	and if he walks before that time, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if hot abscesses occur, then you must soothe it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	of the fingers
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the fingers are dislocated, they must be gently extended without effort, and that is an easy thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in any knot of the back of the foot, then you must have the patient sit on a level place or on a completely straight table, and place your foot on what is visible of those joints, then press firmly with your foot until it returns;
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie;	and when it is even, and nothing appears there, then place a two-legged table under the sole of the foot, then bind it tightly, and leave it for three days, then unbind it;
et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and make him rest until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound occurs with the dislocation, and one wants to restore it, many times it happens that the patient dies:
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	so do not be presumptuous in the treatment, if you are not wise in the art and you have not practiced it for a long time, and if you are not patient and merciful and slow, not rash;
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and use at the beginning of things soothing warm poultices, and leave the patient in God's hands, if you see no hope of health;
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see hope, then immediately restore the limb to its place, before the warm poultices arrive there;
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the limb is in place, then administer soothing warm poultices, and treat the wound, as is appropriate, with drying ointments;
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones separated, then remove them, and do what we have said in simple illnesses;
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	and guard yourself from entering a path of fear, according to what I have said, for that is worth more to you according to your Creator, and for the salvation of your soul and your body.
